110110\nBON_03 ,  100100 110110 110110\nBON_04 ,  100100 110110 110110\nPop\nTAG_01 ,  120120 110110 110110\nTAG_02 ,  120120 110110 110110\nTAG_03 ,  120120 110110 110110\nTAG_04 ,  120120 110110 110110\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn both formats each row is read in as a single character vector. Sample IDs have the population and sample number separated by a \"_\". Between sample ID and the loci is conventional Genepop separator \"   , \" \u003cem\u003e(space,space space)\u003c/em\u003e. Note if your population label is note separated from the sample number in the Sample IDs refer to the help section for . \u003ca href=\"#subsetrenm\"\u003e subset_genepop_rename \u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e Note \u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/span\u003e that input and output \"\u003cstrong\u003epath\u003c/strong\u003e\" variables all require the \u003cstrong\u003eFULL\u003c/strong\u003e file path. Relative paths will not work with \u003cem\u003egenepopedit\u003c/em\u003e functions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMost molecular based file formats can be converted to and from \u003cem\u003eGenepop\u003c/em\u003e using conversion programs such as the R package \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/thibautjombart/adegenet/wiki\"\u003eadegenet\u003c/a\u003e or the program \u003ca href=\"http://www.cmpg.unibe.ch/software/PGDSpider/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ePGDspider\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eInstallation\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-installation\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Installation\" href=\"#installation\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou can install \u003cstrong\u003egenepopedit\u003c/strong\u003e as a R package using the following 2 steps. Before installation it is recommended that you open up a new R session without any packages loaded. During the devtools installation process some package dependencies may be downloaded or updated. Installation errors can arise if an older version of a package dependency is already loaded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStep 1\u003c/strong\u003e Install the \u003cem\u003eR\u003c/em\u003e package \u003cem\u003edevtools\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"if (!require(\u0026quot;devtools\u0026quot;)) install.packages(\u0026quot;devtools\u0026quot;) # to install\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eif\u003c/span\u003e (\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e!\u003c/span\u003erequire(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003edevtools\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e)) install.packages(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003edevtools\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e) \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e#\u003c/span\u003e to install\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStep 2\u003c/strong\u003e Install \u003cem\u003egenepopedit\u003c/em\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"#install the diveRsity dependency from Github ** this package may no longer be supported by CRAN, depending on your R Version **\n#install the package from *Github*\ndevtools::install_github(\u0026quot;kkeenan02/diveRsity\u0026quot;)\ndevtools::install_github(\u0026quot;rystanley/genepopedit\u0026quot;) \nlibrary(genepopedit) # This function will enable R to interact with PGDspider to convert among file formats not included in \u003cstrong\u003egenepopedit\u003c/strong\u003e conversion functions. Currently this is best accomplished using the .spid files generated by PGDspider to define the conversion process. Once a .spid file is created, \u003cstrong\u003egenepopedit\u003c/strong\u003e can continue to convert files provided the conversion parameters in the .spid file match those required for the conversion. \u003cstrong\u003egenepopedit\u003c/strong\u003e require that the population and sample number be separated by an _ in the sample ID (e.g. BON_01 not BON01). This can be accomplished manually using a text editor or using the function \u003cstrong\u003egenepop_ID\u003c/strong\u003e. genepop_ID will read in a Genepop file and look for a common character string within the sample ID vectors grouped by the Genepop \"Pop\" labels. This function assumes that there \u003cem\u003eis\u003c/em\u003e a common string which unifies IDs between each of the Pop labels. If this isn't the case, some pre-filtering of the data using a text editor will be required. \u003ca href=\"#funcmanip\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eFunction description\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"#Use genepop_ID to fix the sample IDs prior to the use of genepopedit functions.\nfilepath=\u0026quot;~myfile.txt\u0026quot; #path to 'myfile' which has sample IDs without the required _ separation. dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis function will calculate linkage disequilibrium and global Weir and Cockerham's Fst for loci among populations. The function seeks a loci panel which maximizes global Fst for unlinked loci. The returned object is a list containing Linked loci ($Linked), global FST ($FST) and the top unlinked loci by FST ($FST_Unlinked). Note 'linked' loci are calcuated based on the threshold R\u003csup\u003e2\u003c/sup\u003e of 0.2 used by PLINK. This threshold (0-1) can be adjusted, though values \u0026lt;0.2 may be limited by computational resources. Note that the available RAM for conversions using PGDspider is limited to 1 GB on Windows based operating systems. For the time being, this function only works with \u003cstrong\u003ePlink 1.9\u003c/strong\u003e. Use of Plink 2.0 will create function issues. \u003ca href=\"#funcdiag\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eFunction description\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWarning messages \u0026amp; diagnostics will be returned to the console by PGDspider \u0026amp; PLINK. These warnings are expected.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" required for the software \u003ca href=\"https://www.zsl.org/science/software/colony\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eColony\u003c/a\u003e. Returned are functions for translating the Colony output and those required by the maximum likelihood analysis. 'Individual' and 'Loci' conversion files can be used to match the loci and individual names formatted for input to Colony to those provided as input by the user.'MarkerTypeErrorRT' file defines the allele dropout rates as calculated using the 'missing' function in PLINK. Rates of other error types are assumed to be equal to the estimated allele dropout rates. 'GENOTYPES' are the geneotypes in two columns per loci format. Output from Colony is based on the input for of the\n'GENOTYPES' file. Original loci and individual names can be assigned using the conversion output files. All files are returned to path and are named according tot he input filename. \u003ca href=\"#funcconvert\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eFunction 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003egenepopedit\u003c/strong\u003e is one of the few tools available to convert data to the format required for input into the Treemix format. It creates a gzipped file that clusters your individuals based on the population ID of the individual's code. Population IDs are extracted using the \"_\" to differentiate population from sample ID (e.g. BON_01 is population BON sample 01). If samples are not separated refer to \u003ca href=\"#genepopidfix\"\u003e\u003cem\u003egenepop_ID\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e. Grouping levels for populations can also be changed using \u003ca href=\"#subsetrenm\"\u003e\u003cem\u003esubset_genepop_rename\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e. Note that this is just the first of two steps in the process; the gzipped output from this function needs to be run through the Python script (Python 2.7+ must be installed first) that accompanies Treemix. This output from \"plink2treemix.py\" is then ready to run in Treemix. This Python script can be downloaded from \u003ca href=\"https://bitbucket.org/nygcresearch/treemix/downloads\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003elink\u003c/a\u003e.  \u003ca href=\"https://bitbucket.org/nygcresearch/treemix/wiki/Home\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eTreemix\u003c/a\u003e is used to infer migration weight and directionality among your populations, as well as detecting population splits and mixtures. \u003ca href=\"#funcconvert\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eFunction description\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight dir=\"auto\"\u003eIndividual geneotypes can be simulated using the \u003cem\u003ealleleotype_genepop()\u003c/em\u003e function and formatted to GENEPOP for use in conventional genomic analyses (e.g. assigner, DAPC, STRUCTURE). This function will simulate individuals for each population provided by the input file. The output can then be diagnosed, sampled, and formatted using other \u003cstrong\u003egenepopedit functions\u003c/strong\u003e. \u003ca href=\"#pooleddna\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eFunction description\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"#simulate individual geneotypes allele frequencies stratified by population.\n  #Create an example pooled DNA input file\n    pooledDNA \u0026lt;- data.frame(Pop = c(\u0026quot;Pop1\u0026quot;,\u0026quot;Pop2\u0026quot;,\u0026quot;Pop3\u0026quot;,\u0026quot;Pop4\u0026quot;,\u0026quot;Pop5\u0026quot;),Loci1 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci2 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci3 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci4 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci5 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci6 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2))\n    \n    #inspect the input\n    pooledDNA\n\n  #simulate 200 individual geneotypes for each population\n    alleleotype_genepop(pooledDNA, numsim = 200, path = paste0(output_dir,\u0026quot;SimulatedGeneotypes.txt\u0026quot;))\n  \n  #To validate output simulate 100 (default) geneotypes per population and compare allele frequencies to those of the input file. genepopedit","[![Travis-CI Build Status](https://travis-ci.org/rystanley/genepopedit.svg?branch=master)](https://travis-ci.org/rystanley/genepopedit)","[![AppVeyor Build Status](https://ci.appveyor.com/api/projects/status/github/rystanley/genepopedit?branch=master\u0026svg=true)](https://ci.appveyor.com/project/rystanley/genepopedit)","[![CRAN_Status_Badge](http://www.r-pkg.org/badges/version/genepopedit)](http://cran.r-project.org/package=genepopedit)","[![DOI](https://zenodo.org/badge/19199/rystanley/genepopedit.svg)](https://zenodo.org/badge/latestdoi/19199/rystanley/genepopedit)","","The goal of **genepopedit** is to provide a simple and flexible tool for manipulating large multi-locus genotype datasets in R. ","","** **Note input parameters for genepopedit versions \u003e 1.0.0.5 are now all completely lowercase.** ** ","","** funciton genepop_toploci() is currently deprecated due to the package diveRsity being no longer maintained.**","","**Use genepopedit to subset a SNP dataset by:**","","* removing specified loci. ","","* removing specified populations. ","","* removing specified individuals.","","* renaming populations. ","","* grouping populations.","","* reordering populations.","","* extracting meta-data:","    * population names.","    * population counts.","    * sample IDs.","    * loci names.","    * allele calls.","    * allele frequencies by population grouping.","    * loci linkage and global Weir and Cockerham's Fst. ","    * lists of unlinked loci maximizing pairwise global Weir and Cockerham's Fst.","    ","* create datasets for training, assignment, and outlier detection, according to a population stratified random sample. ","","* convert Genepop to STRUCTURE, FSTAT, NEWHYBRIDS, ASSIGNER, BGC, TREEMIX, COLONY, Genetic Stock Identification (gsi_sim), HZAR, and flattened/unflattened format.","","* simulate individual genotypes using pooled DNA allele frequencies.","","","***","","![workflow-diagram](inst/doc/vignette_small.png)","","__Fig 1.__ **genepopedit** *workflow including data preparation, diagnostics, manipulation and transformation. Files, functions, and function operations are denoted by black, grey and blue text, respectively. Function inputs and outputs are denoted by dashed and solid lines, respectively.*","","***","**Requirement:**","genepopedit functions through the manipulation of multi-locus diploid SNP files structured in the *Genepop* file format [link](http://genepop.curtin.edu.au/). Specifically, we use the _three number_ format (e.g. 110110) where the six digits correspond to the alleles of a given locus for an individual. Locus names can be listed in the first row separated by columns or each on their own row so that the total number of rows in the _Genepop_ file equals: ","","    nrows = nLOCI + nINDIVIDUALS + nPOPULATIONS - 1","    ","  _or_","  ","    nrows* = nLOCI + nINDIVIDUALS + nPOPULATIONS ","    ","_* if STACKS version is not specified_","","**For example:**","","*A three locus dataset with two populations and four individuals per population with the STACKS version specified*","","    STACKS Version 1.0","    Loci_1","    Loci_2","    Loci_3","    Pop","    BON_01 ,  120120 110110 110110","    BON_02 ,  100100 110110 110110","    BON_03 ,  100100 110110 110110","    BON_04 ,  100100 110110 110110","    Pop","    TAG_01 ,  120120 110110 110110","    TAG_02 ,  120120 110110 110110","    TAG_03 ,  120120 110110 110110","    TAG_04 ,  120120 110110 110110","","Alternatively, the loci names can be read in the first row as a single character separated by commas. ","","    Loci_1,Loci_2,Loci,3","    Pop","    BON_01 ,  120120 110110 110110","    BON_02 ,  100100 110110 110110","    BON_03 ,  100100 110110 110110","    BON_04 ,  100100 110110 110110","    Pop","    TAG_01 ,  120120 110110 110110","    TAG_02 ,  120120 110110 110110","    TAG_03 ,  120120 110110 110110","    TAG_04 ,  120120 110110 110110","    ","In both formats each row is read in as a single character vector. Sample IDs have the population and sample number separated by a \"_\". Between sample ID and the loci is conventional Genepop separator \"   , \" *(space,space space)*. Note if your population label is note separated from the sample number in the Sample IDs refer to the help section for . [ subset\\_genepop\\_rename ](#subsetrenm)","","\u003cspan style=\"color:red\"\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003e Note \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/STRONG\u003e that input and output \"**path**\" variables all require the **FULL** file path. Relative paths will not work with _genepopedit_ functions.  ","","Most molecular based file formats can be converted to and from *Genepop* using conversion programs such as the R package [adegenet](https://github.com/thibautjombart/adegenet/wiki) or the program [PGDspider](http://www.cmpg.unibe.ch/software/PGDSpider/). ","","***","","## Installation","You can install **genepopedit** as a R package using the following 2 steps. Before installation it is recommended that you open up a new R session without any packages loaded. During the devtools installation process some package dependencies may be downloaded or updated. Installation errors can arise if an older version of a package dependency is already loaded.  ","","**Step 1** Install the _R_ package *devtools*","```r","if (!require(\"devtools\")) install.packages(\"devtools\") # to install","```","","**Step 2** Install *genepopedit*:","```r","#install the diveRsity dependency from Github ** this package may no longer be supported by CRAN, depending on your R Version **","#install the package from *Github*","devtools::install_github(\"kkeenan02/diveRsity\")","devtools::install_github(\"rystanley/genepopedit\") ","library(genepopedit) # load the library","```","","\u003ca name=\"extrainstall\"/\u003e","\u003ca name=\"pgdinstall\"/\u003e","","**Step 3** Install *PGDspider* and *plink*. Note these programs are required for the use of **genepop_toploc()** and **PGDspideR()** only!","","  * PGDspider [link](http://www.cmpg.unibe.ch/software/PGDSpider/)","  * plink [link](http://pngu.mgh.harvard.edu/~purcell/plink/download.shtml)","","For the time being, this function only works with **Plink 1.9**. Use of Plink 2.0 will create function issues.","  ","  ","** Note that appveyor build 'failure' is linked to an error in the build check and not *genepopedit* itself. This package has been tested on Windows, Linux (Unbuntu \u0026 Mint), and IOS operating systems. **","","***","","## Contributions:","*genepopedit* was written in collaboration:","  ","  * Ryan Stanley \u003chttps://github.com/rystanley\u003e - Corresponding developer and maintainer","  * Ian Bradbury \u003chttps://bradburygeneticslab.com/\u003e","  * Nick Jeffery \u003chttps://github.com/NickJeff13\u003e","  * Brendan Wringe \u003chttps://github.com/bwringe\u003e","  * Sarah Lehnert \u003chttps://github.com/SarahLehnert\u003e","","Support funding was inpart provided by the Canadian Healthy Oceans Nework [CHONe](https://chone2.ca)","","![](inst/doc/CHONeLogo.jpg)","","This package has been developed to be used by anyone who is looking for a more efficient and **repeatable** method to manipulate large multi-locus datasets. The package is open, and I encourage you to tinker and look for improvements. I will do my best to respond to any inquiries, add additional functions _and-or_ functionality, and improve the efficiency of the package.","","* If you don’t understand something, please let me know: ","(ryan.stanley _at_ dfo-mpo.gc.ca). ","* Any ideas on how to improve the functionality are very much appreciated. ","* If you spot a typo, feel free to edit and send a pull request.","","Pull request how-to: ","","  * Click the edit this page on the sidebar.","  * Make the changes using github’s in-page editor and save.","  * Submit a pull request and include a brief description of your changes. (e.g. \"_spelling errors_\" or \"_indexing error_\").","  ","***","","# **Citation** ","","Full package description and citation now available at **Molecular Ecology Resources** \u003chttp://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/1755-0998.12569/abstract\u003e","","A Zenodo DOI is also avaiable for the most recent release of **genepopedit**:","[![DOI](https://zenodo.org/badge/19199/rystanley/genepopedit.svg)](https://zenodo.org/badge/latestdoi/19199/rystanley/genepopedit)","","***","# **Diagnostics** \u003ca name=\"funcdiag\"/\u003e","","#### genepop_detective.R","","* extract quick meta-data from Genepop file","    * Population names","    * Population counts","    * Sample IDs","    * Loci","    * Alleles","    ","[_example use_](#genepopdetect)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.  ","**variable** | variable to report.","","  * variable=\"Pops\" -\u003e returns vector of population names (default)","  * variable=\"PopNum\" -\u003e returns population summary table","  * variable=\"Loci\" -\u003e returns vector of loci names","  * variable=\"Inds\" -\u003e returns vector of Sample IDs","  * variable=\"All\" -\u003e returns an s4 container with \"Pops\",\"Loci\",\"Inds\" \u0026 \"PopNum\"","  * variable=\"Allele\" -\u003e returns vector of Alleles (*note this might include missing values)","  ","#### genepop_allelefreq.R","Calculate allele frequencies (major) for a given set of loci aggregated by population grouping. ","","[_example use_](#genepopafreq)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.  ","**popgroup** | population grouping using the \"Pop\" delimiter (Default: NULL) or a dataframe or path to a csv. The grouping dataframe should have two columns, the first corresponding to the population name and the second to an aggregation vector of common groups. Each population can only be assigned to one group.","**wide** | logical (default: FALSE) defining whether the output should be cast in 'wide' format. Note that 'wide' format is accepted as the input for alleleotype_genepop().","","#### genepop_filter_maf.R","Filter loci by global minor allele frequency. For the time being, this function only works with **Plink 1.9**. Use of Plink 2.0 will create function issues.","","[_example use_](#genepopmaf)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.  ","**where.plink** | A file path to the PLINK installation folder.","**where.pgdspider** | A file path to the PGDspider installation folder.","**maf** | Minor allele frequency cutoff (default = 0.05)","**path** | the filepath \u0026 filename of output.","","#### genepop_toploci.R","This function will return the the panel with the highest Fst for unlinked loci ordered by Fst. Returned loci have the highest Fst from the _original panel_ and are not linked to any other loci in the _returned panel_. Note this function requires the installation and access to both PGDspider for format conversion \u0026 PLINK for linkage calculations. For the time being, this function only works with **Plink 1.9**. Use of Plink 2.0 will create function issues. [_See installation instructions here_](#extrainstall)","","[_example use_](#genepoptoploc)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | A path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.  ","**where.plink** | A file path to the PLINK installation folder.","**where.pgdspider** | A file path to the PGDspider installation folder.","**r2.theshold** | Linkage threshold based on correlation between loci. Value must be between 0 \u0026 1. Default: 0.2 matched to PLINK defaults. ","**fst.threshold** | The minimum r^2 threshold to consider a pair of loci to be considered linked (default: 0.05).","**ld.window** | The number of sequential loci to be considered for linkage. This sliding window is based on the input order of loci in the input data. Default (NULL) will calcualte linkage among **all loci**. This variable should not be changed unless the order and proximity of loci on the genome is known and integrated into the order within the input data.","**ldpop** | A string which denotes which of the populations you wish to calculate linkage disequilibrium from. The default is to calculate LD among all (\"All\") populations. Population names must match those returned by [*genepop_detective*](#genepopdetect).","**allocate.pgd.ram** | An integer defining how many GB of ram will be made available to PGD spider during calculation of LD. Default (1 GB) should be sufficient for most calculations. Note that for Windows based platforms the limitation for PGDspider is ~1 GB. If a value other than default is specified on Windows _allocate.pgd.ram_ will be set to 1 GB.","**return.workspace** | Logical query (default: TRUE) sepecifying whether to return the output to the workspace.","**save.output** | Logical query (default: FALSE) to save the output to the same location as the file being analyzed. Each of the outputs of the function will be saved as a separate file with the file name of the orginal data appended with \"Linkages\", \"Loci-FST\", and \"Unlinked-Loci-FST\" for the pairwise linked loci along with their r^2, all loci with their global Fst, and only the top unlinked loci with their Fst respectively.","","***","","# **Manipulation** \u003ca name=\"funcmanip\"/\u003e","","#### subset_genepop.R ","* remove or keep a subset of loci ","* remove populations ","","[_example use_](#subsetgenp)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.","**subs** | vector loci names of interest (default: NULL)","**keep** | logical whether to keep loci specified by subs (default: TRUE) or to keep remaining loci.","**spop** | populations to be retained (default: NULL).","**path** | the filepath \u0026 filename of output.","","#### subset_genepop_rename.R","* subset and-or rename populations","","[_example use_](#subsetrenm)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.","**nameframe** | a dataframe or path to a csv detailing the original and any edited population names or sampleIDs.","**renumber** | logical (default: FALSE) whether the sample numbers are to be replaced. ","**meta** | character defining which meta information is being edited. Options are \"Pop\" (default) or \"Ind\" for populations or sampleIDs respectively. This parameter must be specified.","**path** | the filepath \u0026 filename of output.","","#### subset_genepop_aggregate.R","* group populations based on Genepop population tags","","[_example use_](#subsetagg)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.","**subs** | vector loci names of interest (default: NULL)","**keep** | logical whether to keep loci specified by subs (default: TRUE) or to keep remaining loci.","**agpopframe** | a dataframe or path to a csv detailing the population names \u0026 populations to be aggregated.","**path** | the filepath \u0026 filename of output.","","#### subset_genepop_individuals.R","* remove or keep a subset of individuals","","[_example use_](#subsetidv)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.","**indiv** | vector sample IDs of interest.","**keep** | logical whether to delete sample IDs specified by indiv (default: TRUE) or delete all other IDs.","**path** | the filepath \u0026 filename of output.","","#### genepop_ID.R","* function to add '_' between the population and sample number of a sample ID. This format (e.g. BON_01) is required for the remaining genepopedit functions. If your data already fits this format then this function need not be used. ","","[_example use_](#genepopidfix)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|-----------------------------------","**genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.","**path** | the filepath \u0026 filename of output.","","#### genepop_reorder.R ","* Return genepop file with populations ordered sequentially according to specified population order. ","","[_example use_](#genepopreorder)","  ","  **Variable name** | **Input**  ","    --------------|---------------------------------","    **genepop** | a path to a Genepop file _or_ a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.","    **reorder** | vector of populaton names which will be used to reorder the output file. ","**path** | the filepath \u0026 filename of output.","","***","","### Conversion using PGDspider \u003ca name=\"funcpgd\"/\u003e","","We have developed an _R_ interface for [PGDspider](http://www.cmpg.unibe.ch/software/PGDSpider/). This function will enable R to interact with PGDspider to convert among file formats not included in **genepopedit** conversion functions. Currently this is best accomplished using the .spid files generated by PGDspider to define the conversion process. Once a .spid file is created, **genepopedit** can continue to convert files provided the conversion parameters in the .spid file match those required for the conversion. This program will require installation of PGDspider. [_See installation instructions here_](#pgdinstall)","","#### PGDspideR.R","* call conversion tools of pgdSpider through R","","[_example use_](#pgdspiderConvert)","","**Variable name** | **Input**  ","--------------|---------------------------------","**input** | complete file path to the input file to be converted. ","```","If reading in data to your workspace use the following *read.table* code specifics and associated parameters (sep=\"\\t\",quote=\"\",stringsAsFactors=FALSE)","","```r","#Example file path to your data","  file.link \u003c- \"c:/Users/YOUR NAME/Documents/Data/genepopdata.txt\"","","#If your dataset has fewer than ~15,000 loci *read.table* should suffice","  GenePop \u003c- read.table(file.link,sep=\"\\t\",quote=\"\",stringsAsFactors=FALSE)","","#If your dataset has a large amount of loci (\u003e15,000) then we suggest using the data.table package to load in the data more efficiently.","  GenePop \u003c- data.table::fread(file.link,header=FALSE, sep=\"\\t\",stringsAsFactors=FALSE)","```","","However, reading in your GENEPOP data into the workspace is not required, as all functions can work with both workspace objects *and* **file paths**.","","Set a directory where the output files will be saved.","","```r","output_dir \u003c- \"c:/Users/YourName/Documents/GenePopFiles/\" ","```","","***","","# **Preparation** \u003ca name=\"genepopidfix\"/\u003e","","## genepop\\_ID","Functions available in **genepopedit** require that the population and sample number be separated by an _ in the sample ID (e.g. BON_01 not BON01). This can be accomplished manually using a text editor or using the function **genepop_ID**. genepop_ID will read in a Genepop file and look for a common character string within the sample ID vectors grouped by the Genepop \"Pop\" labels. This function assumes that there _is_ a common string which unifies IDs between each of the Pop labels. If this isn't the case, some pre-filtering of the data using a text editor will be required. [_Function description_](#funcmanip)","","```r","#Use genepop_ID to fix the sample IDs prior to the use of genepopedit functions.","filepath=\"~myfile.txt\" #path to 'myfile' which has sample IDs without the required _ separation. Note this can also be an object in the workspace.","","genepop_ID(genepop=filepath, path=paste0(output_dir,\"Genepop_SampleID_fixed.txt\"))","```","","***","","# **Diagnostics** \u003ca name=\"genepopdetect\"/\u003e","","## genepop\\_detective","This function queries meta-data from your genepop data without having to open it in a text editor. The function seeks a loci panel which maximizes global Fst for unlinked loci. The returned object is a list containing Linked loci ($Linked), global FST ($FST) and the top unlinked loci by FST ($FST_Unlinked). Note 'linked' loci are calcuated based on the threshold R\u003csup\u003e2\u003c/sup\u003e of 0.2 used by PLINK. This threshold (0-1) can be adjusted, though values \u003c0.2 may be limited by computational resources. Note that the available RAM for conversions using PGDspider is limited to 1 GB on Windows based operating systems. For the time being, this function only works with **Plink 1.9**. [_Function description_](#funcsamp)","","```r","#view how many individuals you have in each population","  genepop_detective(GenePopData,\"PopNum\")","```","There are several ways we can sub-sample each population","","Use a fixed number (e.g. 5 from each population)","```r","  SubSamp \u003c- genepop_sample(GenePopData, nsample = 5)","```","","*or*","","","Use a fixed fraction (e.g. 25% from each population)","```r","  SubSamp \u003c- genepop_sample(GenePopData, nsample = 0.25)","```","","*or*","","Use a fraction which varies for each population","```r","#vector of populations in the Genepop file","  Pops \u003c- genepop_detective(GenePopData,\"Pops\")","","#create a dataframe which defines how many you want to sample from each population. Note here we create a column which has an entry for each population.","  subdf \u003c- data.frame(Pops = Pops, nsample = c(5, 2, 3, 5, 6, 5, 2, 3, 5, 6)/10)","","  SubSamp \u003c- genepop_sample(GenePopData, nsample = subdf)","```","","Once you select a method to sub-sample each population, you can use the function subset-genepop-indiv to create the sampled genepop file.","","For example if you wanted to create a training and assignment dataset  in genepop format using the random stratified sampled we selected using subset-genepop-indiv:","","```r","#Create training dataset (keep = TRUE)","  subset_genepop_individual(GenePopData, indiv = SubSamp, keep = TRUE, path = paste0(output_dir,\"Genepop_training.txt\"))","","#Create an assignment dataset using the remaining individuals (keep = FALSE)","  subset_genepop_individual(GenePopData, indiv = SubSamp, keep = FALSE, path = paste0(output_dir,\"Genepop_assignment.txt\"))","```","","***","","# **Conversion**","","","## genepop\\_structure \u003ca name=\"genepopstruc\"/\u003e","If you are interested in investigating population structure you can convert your modified Genepop object or path to saved file directly into a [STRUCTURE](http://web.stanford.edu/group/pritchardlab/structure.html) formatted text (.str) file \u003c\u003e. name=\"genepopcolony\"/\u003e","If you are interested in investigating sibship or parentage, you can convert to the format required for the software [Colony](https://www.zsl.org/science/software/colony). Returned are functions for translating the Colony output and those required by the maximum likelihood analysis. 'Individual' and 'Loci' conversion files can be used to match the loci and individual names formatted for input to Colony to those provided as input by the user.'MarkerTypeErrorRT' file defines the allele dropout rates as calculated using the 'missing' function in PLINK. Rates of other error types are assumed to be equal to the estimated allele dropout rates. 'GENOTYPES' are the geneotypes in two columns per loci format. Output from Colony is based on the input for of the "," 'GENOTYPES' file. Original loci and individual names can be assigned using the conversion output files. BGC can evalute genomic clinal patterns and introgression among loci. To convert to BGC format you must specify which populations you consider to be ancestral or **parental** (P1, P2) and which you assume could be hybridized (**admixed**). [_Function description_](#funcconvert)","","```r","#specify which populations are going to be included in the analysis and to which class they belong. It creates a gzipped file that clusters your individuals based on the population ID of the individual's code. Population IDs are extracted using the \"_\" to differentiate population from sample ID (e.g. BON_01 is population BON sample 01). If samples are not separated refer to [_genepop_ID_](#genepopidfix). Grouping levels for populations can also be changed using [_subset_genepop_rename_](#subsetrenm). Note that this is just the first of two steps in the process; the gzipped output from this function needs to be run through the Python script (Python 2.7+ must be installed first) that accompanies Treemix. This output from \"plink2treemix.py\" is then ready to run in Treemix. This Python script can be downloaded from [link](https://bitbucket.org/nygcresearch/treemix/downloads).  [Treemix](https://bitbucket.org/nygcresearch/treemix/wiki/Home) is used to infer migration weight and directionality among your populations, as well as detecting population splits and mixtures. [_Function description_](#funcconvert)","","```r","","#convert Genepop to Treemix input and keep intermediary conversion files (default: FALSE)","  genepop_treemix(genepop=\"Genepop_IDsubset.txt\",where.plink=\"c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/plink/\",where.pgdspider=\"c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/PGDSpider_2.0.9.0/\",keep_inter = TRUE, path = paste0(output_dir,\"Treemix_IDsubset.txt\"))","","```","","## genepop\\_GSIsim \u003ca name=\"genepopgsi\"/\u003e","If you are interested in assessing the accuracy of a genetic stock identification analysis, given a genetic baseline, you can convert directly from GENEPOP to a GSI_sim formatted text file. **genepopedit** is among the few tools currenlty available to format data for GSI_sim. class="BlobViewContent-module__blobContentWrapper__JS0W6"><section aria-labelledby="file-name-id-wide file-name-id-mobile" class="BlobContent-module__blobContentSection__VOgZq BlobContent-module__blobContentSectionMarkdown__mPLOK" style="margin-top:46px"><div class="js-snippet-clipboard-copy-unpositioned BlobContent-module__markdownBlob__T8jpG" data-hpc="true"><article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepopedit</h1><a id="user-content-genepopedit" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepopedit" href="#genepopedit"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://travis-ci.org/rystanley/genepopedit" rel="nofollow"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/a0c71399a0093eddb420a874511d90f1bc7c697066bcd3dd55de5f380bef2aec/68747470733a2f2f7472617669732d63692e6f72672f72797374616e6c65792f67656e65706f70656469742e7376673f6272616e63683d6d6173746572" alt="Travis-CI Build Status" data-canonical-src="https://travis-ci.org/rystanley/genepopedit.svg?branch=master" style="max-width: 100%;"></a>
<a href="https://ci.appveyor.com/project/rystanley/genepopedit" rel="nofollow"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/9a8cd5a63811468242c98e783ceb426722a51fcb7af33ca9507c5e28b4735389/68747470733a2f2f63692e6170707665796f722e636f6d2f6170692f70726f6a656374732f7374617475732f6769746875622f72797374616e6c65792f67656e65706f70656469743f6272616e63683d6d6173746572267376673d74727565" alt="AppVeyor Build Status" data-canonical-src="https://ci.appveyor.com/api/projects/status/github/rystanley/genepopedit?branch=master&amp;svg=true" style="max-width: 100%;"></a>
<a href="http://cran.r-project.org/package=genepopedit" rel="nofollow"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/5e4eee1d571f5df1580bb36bcb524a7ce856e981c682735e704b0e179642cbfd/687474703a2f2f7777772e722d706b672e6f72672f6261646765732f76657273696f6e2f67656e65706f7065646974" alt="CRAN_Status_Badge" data-canonical-src="http://www.r-pkg.org/badges/version/genepopedit" style="max-width: 100%;"></a>
<a href="https://zenodo.org/badge/latestdoi/19199/rystanley/genepopedit" rel="nofollow"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/ff4c4de65e9734b2a17414c9e478fb278e332d8ac13b6d1d7f5bd00cd454b46a/68747470733a2f2f7a656e6f646f2e6f72672f62616467652f31393139392f72797374616e6c65792f67656e65706f70656469742e737667" alt="DOI" data-canonical-src="https://zenodo.org/badge/19199/rystanley/genepopedit.svg" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The goal of <strong>genepopedit</strong> is to provide a simple and flexible tool for manipulating large multi-locus genotype datasets in R.</p>
<p dir="auto">** <strong>Note input parameters for genepopedit versions &gt; 1.0.0.5 are now all completely lowercase.</strong> **</p>
<p dir="auto">** funciton genepop_toploci() is currently deprecated due to the package diveRsity being no longer maintained.**</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Use genepopedit to subset a SNP dataset by:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">removing specified loci.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">removing specified populations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">removing specified individuals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">renaming populations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">grouping populations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">reordering populations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">extracting meta-data:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>population names.</li>
<li>population counts.</li>
<li>sample IDs.</li>
<li>loci names.</li>
<li>allele calls.</li>
<li>allele frequencies by population grouping.</li>
<li>loci linkage and global Weir and Cockerham's Fst.</li>
<li>lists of unlinked loci maximizing pairwise global Weir and Cockerham's Fst.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">create datasets for training, assignment, and outlier detection, according to a population stratified random sample.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">convert Genepop to STRUCTURE, FSTAT, NEWHYBRIDS, ASSIGNER, BGC, TREEMIX, COLONY, Genetic Stock Identification (gsi_sim), HZAR, and flattened/unflattened format.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">simulate individual genotypes using pooled DNA allele frequencies.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<hr>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/rystanley/genepopedit/blob/master/inst/doc/vignette_small.png"><img src="/rystanley/genepopedit/raw/master/inst/doc/vignette_small.png" alt="workflow-diagram" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Fig 1.</strong> <strong>genepopedit</strong> <em>workflow including data preparation, diagnostics, manipulation and transformation. Files, functions, and function operations are denoted by black, grey and blue text, respectively. Function inputs and outputs are denoted by dashed and solid lines, respectively.</em></p>
<hr>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Requirement:</strong>
genepopedit functions through the manipulation of multi-locus diploid SNP files structured in the <em>Genepop</em> file format <a href="http://genepop.curtin.edu.au/" rel="nofollow">link</a>. Specifically, we use the <em>three number</em> format (e.g. 110110) where the six digits correspond to the alleles of a given locus for an individual. Locus names can be listed in the first row separated by columns or each on their own row so that the total number of rows in the <em>Genepop</em> file equals:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="nrows = nLOCI + nINDIVIDUALS + nPOPULATIONS - 1"><pre class="notranslate"><code>nrows = nLOCI + nINDIVIDUALS + nPOPULATIONS - 1
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><em>or</em></p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="nrows* = nLOCI + nINDIVIDUALS + nPOPULATIONS "><pre class="notranslate"><code>nrows* = nLOCI + nINDIVIDUALS + nPOPULATIONS 
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><em>* if STACKS version is not specified</em></p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>For example:</strong></p>
<p dir="auto"><em>A three locus dataset with two populations and four individuals per population with the STACKS version specified</em></p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="STACKS Version 1.0
Loci_1
Loci_2
Loci_3
Pop
BON_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
BON_02 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_03 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_04 ,  100100 110110 110110
Pop
TAG_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_02 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_03 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_04 ,  120120 110110 110110"><pre class="notranslate"><code>STACKS Version 1.0
Loci_1
Loci_2
Loci_3
Pop
BON_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
BON_02 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_03 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_04 ,  100100 110110 110110
Pop
TAG_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_02 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_03 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_04 ,  120120 110110 110110
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Alternatively, the loci names can be read in the first row as a single character separated by commas.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Loci_1,Loci_2,Loci,3
Pop
BON_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
BON_02 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_03 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_04 ,  100100 110110 110110
Pop
TAG_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_02 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_03 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_04 ,  120120 110110 110110"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Loci_1,Loci_2,Loci,3
Pop
BON_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
BON_02 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_03 ,  100100 110110 110110
BON_04 ,  100100 110110 110110
Pop
TAG_01 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_02 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_03 ,  120120 110110 110110
TAG_04 ,  120120 110110 110110
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In both formats each row is read in as a single character vector. Sample IDs have the population and sample number separated by a "_". Between sample ID and the loci is conventional Genepop separator "   , " <em>(space,space space)</em>. Note if your population label is note separated from the sample number in the Sample IDs refer to the help section for . <a href="#subsetrenm"> subset_genepop_rename </a></p>
<p dir="auto"><span><strong> Note </strong></span> that input and output "<strong>path</strong>" variables all require the <strong>FULL</strong> file path. Relative paths will not work with <em>genepopedit</em> functions.</p>
<p dir="auto">Most molecular based file formats can be converted to and from <em>Genepop</em> using conversion programs such as the R package <a href="https://github.com/thibautjombart/adegenet/wiki">adegenet</a> or the program <a href="http://www.cmpg.unibe.ch/software/PGDSpider/" rel="nofollow">PGDspider</a>.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Installation</h2><a id="user-content-installation" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Installation" href="#installation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">You can install <strong>genepopedit</strong> as a R package using the following 2 steps. Before installation it is recommended that you open up a new R session without any packages loaded. During the devtools installation process some package dependencies may be downloaded or updated. Installation errors can arise if an older version of a package dependency is already loaded.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Step 1</strong> Install the <em>R</em> package <em>devtools</em></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="if (!require(&quot;devtools&quot;)) install.packages(&quot;devtools&quot;) # to install"><pre><span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-k">!</span>require(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>devtools<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)) install.packages(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>devtools<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> to install</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Step 2</strong> Install <em>genepopedit</em>:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#install the diveRsity dependency from Github ** this package may no longer be supported by CRAN, depending on your R Version **
#install the package from *Github*
devtools::install_github(&quot;kkeenan02/diveRsity&quot;)
devtools::install_github(&quot;rystanley/genepopedit&quot;) 
library(genepopedit) # load the library"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>install the diveRsity dependency from Github ** this package may no longer be supported by CRAN, depending on your R Version **</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>install the package from *Github*</span>
<span class="pl-e">devtools</span><span class="pl-k">::</span>install_github(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>kkeenan02/diveRsity<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)
<span class="pl-e">devtools</span><span class="pl-k">::</span>install_github(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>rystanley/genepopedit<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) 
library(<span class="pl-smi">genepopedit</span>) <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> load the library</span></pre></div>
<a name="user-content-extrainstall">
</a><a name="user-content-pgdinstall">
<p dir="auto"><strong>Step 3</strong> Install <em>PGDspider</em> and <em>plink</em>. Note these programs are required for the use of <strong>genepop_toploc()</strong> and <strong>PGDspideR()</strong> only!</p>
</a><ul dir="auto">
<li>PGDspider <a href="http://www.cmpg.unibe.ch/software/PGDSpider/" rel="nofollow">link</a></li>
<li>plink <a href="http://pngu.mgh.harvard.edu/~purcell/plink/download.shtml" rel="nofollow">link</a></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">For the time being, this function only works with <strong>Plink 1.9</strong>. Use of Plink 2.0 will create function issues.</p>
<p dir="auto">** Note that appveyor build 'failure' is linked to an error in the build check and not <em>genepopedit</em> itself. This package has been tested on Windows, Linux (Unbuntu &amp; Mint), and IOS operating systems. **</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Contributions:</h2><a id="user-content-contributions" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Contributions:" href="#contributions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><em>genepopedit</em> was written in collaboration:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Ryan Stanley <a href="https://github.com/rystanley">https://github.com/rystanley</a> - Corresponding developer and maintainer</li>
<li>Ian Bradbury <a href="https://bradburygeneticslab.com/" rel="nofollow">https://bradburygeneticslab.com/</a></li>
<li>Nick Jeffery <a href="https://github.com/NickJeff13">https://github.com/NickJeff13</a></li>
<li>Brendan Wringe <a href="https://github.com/bwringe">https://github.com/bwringe</a></li>
<li>Sarah Lehnert <a href="https://github.com/SarahLehnert">https://github.com/SarahLehnert</a></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Support funding was inpart provided by the Canadian Healthy Oceans Nework <a href="https://chone2.ca" rel="nofollow">CHONe</a></p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/rystanley/genepopedit/blob/master/inst/doc/CHONeLogo.jpg"><img src="/rystanley/genepopedit/raw/master/inst/doc/CHONeLogo.jpg" alt="" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">This package has been developed to be used by anyone who is looking for a more efficient and <strong>repeatable</strong> method to manipulate large multi-locus datasets. The package is open, and I encourage you to tinker and look for improvements. I will do my best to respond to any inquiries, add additional functions <em>and-or</em> functionality, and improve the efficiency of the package.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>If you don’t understand something, please let me know:
(ryan.stanley <em>at</em> dfo-mpo.gc.ca).</li>
<li>Any ideas on how to improve the functionality are very much appreciated.</li>
<li>If you spot a typo, feel free to edit and send a pull request.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Pull request how-to:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Click the edit this page on the sidebar.</li>
<li>Make the changes using github’s in-page editor and save.</li>
<li>Submit a pull request and include a brief description of your changes. (e.g. "<em>spelling errors</em>" or "<em>indexing error</em>").</li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto"><strong>Citation</strong></h1><a id="user-content-citation" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Citation" href="#citation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Full package description and citation now available at <strong>Molecular Ecology Resources</strong> <a href="http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/1755-0998.12569/abstract" rel="nofollow">http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/1755-0998.12569/abstract</a></p>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto"><strong>Diagnostics</strong> <a name="user-content-funcdiag"></a></h1><a id="user-content-diagnostics-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Diagnostics" href="#diagnostics-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_detective.R</h4><a id="user-content-genepop_detectiver" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_detective.R" href="#genepop_detectiver"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>extract quick meta-data from Genepop file
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Population names</li>
<li>Population counts</li>
<li>Sample IDs</li>
<li>Loci</li>
<li>Alleles</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><a href="#genepopdetect"><em>example use</em></a></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th><strong>Variable name</strong></th>
<th><strong>Input</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>genepop</strong></td>
<td>a path to a Genepop file <em>or</em> a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>variable</strong></td>
<td>variable to report.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>variable="Pops" -&gt; returns vector of population names (default)</li>
<li>variable="PopNum" -&gt; returns population summary table</li>
<li>variable="Loci" -&gt; returns vector of loci names</li>
<li>variable="Inds" -&gt; returns vector of Sample IDs</li>
<li>variable="All" -&gt; returns an s4 container with "Pops","Loci","Inds" &amp; "PopNum"</li>
<li>variable="Allele" -&gt; returns vector of Alleles (*note this might include missing values)</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_allelefreq.R</h4><a id="user-content-genepop_allelefreqr" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_allelefreq.R" href="#genepop_allelefreqr"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Calculate allele frequencies (major) for a given set of loci aggregated by population grouping.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="#genepopafreq"><em>example use</em></a></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th><strong>Variable name</strong></th>
<th><strong>Input</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>genepop</strong></td>
<td>a path to a Genepop file <em>or</em> a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>popgroup</strong></td>
<td>population grouping using the "Pop" delimiter (Default: NULL) or a dataframe or path to a csv. The grouping dataframe should have two columns, the first corresponding to the population name and the second to an aggregation vector of common groups. Each population can only be assigned to one group.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>wide</strong></td>
<td>logical (default: FALSE) defining whether the output should be cast in 'wide' format. Note that 'wide' format is accepted as the input for alleleotype_genepop().</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_filter_maf.R</h4><a id="user-content-genepop_filter_mafr" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_filter_maf.R" href="#genepop_filter_mafr"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Filter loci by global minor allele frequency. For the time being, this function only works with <strong>Plink 1.9</strong>. Use of Plink 2.0 will create function issues.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="#genepopmaf"><em>example use</em></a></p>

</tr>

<td><strong>genepop</strong></td>
<td>a path to a Genepop file <em>or</em> a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>where.plink</strong></td>
<td>A file path to the PLINK installation folder.</td>

<td>A file path to the PGDspider installation folder.</td>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_toploci.R</h4><a id="user-content-genepop_toplocir" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_toploci.R" href="#genepop_toplocir"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">This function will return the the panel with the highest Fst for unlinked loci ordered by Fst. Returned loci have the highest Fst from the <em>original panel</em> and are not linked to any other loci in the <em>returned panel</em>. Note this function requires the installation and access to both PGDspider for format conversion &amp; PLINK for linkage calculations. For the time being, this function only works with <strong>Plink 1.9</strong>. Use of Plink 2.0 will create function issues. <a href="#extrainstall"><em>See installation instructions here</em></a></p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="#genepoptoploc"><em>example use</em></a></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th><strong>Variable name</strong></th>
<th><strong>Input</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>genepop</strong></td>
<td>A path to a Genepop file <em>or</em> a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>where.plink</strong></td>
<td>A file path to the PLINK installation folder.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>where.pgdspider</strong></td>
<td>A file path to the PGDspider installation folder.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>r2.theshold</strong></td>
<td>Linkage threshold based on correlation between loci. Value must be between 0 &amp; 1. Default: 0.2 matched to PLINK defaults.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>fst.threshold</strong></td>
<td>The minimum r^2 threshold to consider a pair of loci to be considered linked (default: 0.05).</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>ld.window</strong></td>
<td>The number of sequential loci to be considered for linkage. This sliding window is based on the input order of loci in the input data. Default (NULL) will calcualte linkage among <strong>all loci</strong>. This variable should not be changed unless the order and proximity of loci on the genome is known and integrated into the order within the input data.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>ldpop</strong></td>
<td>A string which denotes which of the populations you wish to calculate linkage disequilibrium from. The default is to calculate LD among all ("All") populations. Population names must match those returned by <a href="#genepopdetect"><em>genepop_detective</em></a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>allocate.pgd.ram</strong></td>
<td>An integer defining how many GB of ram will be made available to PGD spider during calculation of LD. Default (1 GB) should be sufficient for most calculations. Note that for Windows based platforms the limitation for PGDspider is ~1 GB. If a value other than default is specified on Windows <em>allocate.pgd.ram</em> will be set to 1 GB.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>return.workspace</strong></td>
<td>Logical query (default: TRUE) sepecifying whether to return the output to the workspace.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>save.output</strong></td>
<td>Logical query (default: FALSE) to save the output to the same location as the file being analyzed. Each of the outputs of the function will be saved as a separate file with the file name of the orginal data appended with "Linkages", "Loci-FST", and "Unlinked-Loci-FST" for the pairwise linked loci along with their r^2, all loci with their global Fst, and only the top unlinked loci with their Fst respectively.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto"><strong>Manipulation</strong> <a name="user-content-funcmanip"></a></h1><a id="user-content-manipulation-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Manipulation" href="#manipulation-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">subset_genepop.R</h4><a id="user-content-subset_genepopr" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: subset_genepop.R" href="#subset_genepopr"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>remove or keep a subset of loci</li>
<li>remove populations</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><a href="#subsetgenp"><em>example use</em></a></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th><strong>Variable name</strong></th>
<th><strong>Input</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>genepop</strong></td>
<td>a path to a Genepop file <em>or</em> a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>subs</strong></td>
<td>vector loci names of interest (default: NULL)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>keep</strong></td>
<td>logical whether to keep loci specified by subs (default: TRUE) or to keep remaining loci.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>spop</strong></td>
<td>populations to be retained (default: NULL).</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>path</strong></td>
<td>the filepath &amp; filename of output.</td>
</tr>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Variable name</strong> | <strong>Input</strong><br>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_sample.R</h4><a id="user-content-genepop_sampler" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_sample.R" href="#genepop_sampler"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Subsample individuals from a genepop file using population based random stratified sampling.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><a href="#genepopsamp"><em>example use</em></a></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th><strong>Variable name</strong></th>
<th><strong>Input</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>genepop</strong></td>
<td>a path to a Genepop file <em>or</em> a dataframe read into the workspace of a Genepop file</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>nsample</strong></td>
<td>object which defines sampling.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>nsample (integer) -&gt; (e.g. nsample = 5) nsample will be sampled at random from each strata (population).</li>
<li>nsample (fraction) -&gt; (e.g. nsample = 0.5) a fraction will be sampled at random from each strata (population).</li>
<li>nsample (integer per population) -&gt; (e.g. number varying per population) nsample (column 2) will be sampled at random from each strata (column 1 population).</li>
<li>nsample (fraction per population) -&gt; (e.g. fraction varying per population) a fraction (column 2) will be sampled at random from each strata (column 1 population).</li>
</ul>
<hr>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Conversion using PGDspider <a name="user-content-funcpgd"></a></h3><a id="user-content-conversion-using-pgdspider-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Conversion using PGDspider " href="#conversion-using-pgdspider-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">We have developed an <em>R</em> interface for <a href="http://www.cmpg.unibe.ch/software/PGDSpider/" rel="nofollow">PGDspider</a>. This function will enable R to interact with PGDspider to convert among file formats not included in <strong>genepopedit</strong> conversion functions. Currently this is best accomplished using the .spid files generated by PGDspider to define the conversion process. Once a .spid file is created, <strong>genepopedit</strong> can continue to convert files provided the conversion parameters in the .spid file match those required for the conversion. This program will require installation of PGDspider. <a href="#pgdinstall"><em>See installation instructions here</em></a></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">PGDspideR.R</h4><a id="user-content-pgdspiderr" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: PGDspideR.R" href="#pgdspiderr"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>call conversion tools of pgdSpider through R</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><a href="#pgdspiderConvert"><em>example use</em></a></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th><strong>Variable name</strong></th>
<th><strong>Input</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>input</strong></td>
<td>complete file path to the input file to be converted.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>input_format</strong></td>
<td>format of the input file. This format should match the dropdown menus of pgdSpider in terms of spelling and capitalization (e.g. GENEPOP &amp; FSTAT).</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>output</strong></td>
<td>complete file path to the defining where the converted file will be stored.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>output_format</strong></td>
<td>format of the of the converted file. This format should match the dropdown menus of pgdSpider in terms of spelling and capitalization (e.g. GENEPOP &amp; FSTAT).</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>spid</strong></td>
<td>complete file path to the .spid file created by pgdSpider defining the conversion between input_format and output_format. Note that parameters of this .spid file must match the conversion and input file as specified by pgdSpider.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>where.pgdspider</strong></td>
<td>the filepath to the folder where pgdSpider installation files are stored.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
