class="pl-pds">"</span>CCC<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>DDD<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>EEE<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>FFF<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>GGG<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>HHH<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>III<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>JJJ<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>),<span class="pl-v">groups</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> c(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>P1<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>P1<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>P1<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Admixed<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Admixed<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Admixed<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Admixed<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>P2<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>P2<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>P2<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>))

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>convert Genepop to BGC input files (3). Note in this case the variable path is a path to the directory where the input files will be saved.</span>
  genepop_bgc(<span class="pl-v">genepop</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Genepop_IDsubset.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-v">popdef</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">BGC_groups</span>, <span class="pl-v">fname</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>BGC_IDsubset<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-v">path</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">output_dir</span>)
</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_treemix <a name="user-content-genepoptreemix"></a></h2><a id="user-content-genepop_treemix-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_treemix " href="#genepop_treemix-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>genepopedit</strong> is one of the few tools available to convert data to the format required for input into the Treemix format. It creates a gzipped file that clusters your individuals based on the population ID of the individual's code. Population IDs are extracted using the "_" to differentiate population from sample ID (e.g. BON_01 is population BON sample 01). If samples are not separated refer to <a href="#genepopidfix"><em>genepop_ID</em></a>. Grouping levels for populations can also be changed using <a href="#subsetrenm"><em>subset_genepop_rename</em></a>. Note that this is just the first of two steps in the process; the gzipped output from this function needs to be run through the Python script (Python 2.7+ must be installed first) that accompanies Treemix. This output from "plink2treemix.py" is then ready to run in Treemix. This Python script can be downloaded from <a href="https://bitbucket.org/nygcresearch/treemix/downloads" rel="nofollow">link</a>.  <a href="https://bitbucket.org/nygcresearch/treemix/wiki/Home" rel="nofollow">Treemix</a> is used to infer migration weight and directionality among your populations, as well as detecting population splits and mixtures. <a href="#funcconvert"><em>Function description</em></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="
#convert Genepop to Treemix input and keep intermediary conversion files (default: FALSE)
  genepop_treemix(genepop=&quot;Genepop_IDsubset.txt&quot;,where.plink=&quot;c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/plink/&quot;,where.pgdspider=&quot;c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/PGDSpider_2.0.9.0/&quot;,keep_inter = TRUE, path = paste0(output_dir,&quot;Treemix_IDsubset.txt&quot;))
"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>convert Genepop to Treemix input and keep intermediary conversion files (default: FALSE)</span>
  genepop_treemix(<span class="pl-v">genepop</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Genepop_IDsubset.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-v">where.plink</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/plink/<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-v">where.pgdspider</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/PGDSpider_2.0.9.0/<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-v">keep_inter</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">TRUE</span>, <span class="pl-v">path</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> paste0(<span class="pl-smi">output_dir</span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Treemix_IDsubset.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>))
</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_GSIsim <a name="user-content-genepopgsi"></a></h2><a id="user-content-genepop_gsisim-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_GSIsim " href="#genepop_gsisim-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">If you are interested in assessing the accuracy of a genetic stock identification analysis, given a genetic baseline, you can convert directly from GENEPOP to a GSI_sim formatted text file. <strong>genepopedit</strong> is among the few tools currenlty available to format data for GSI_sim. <a href="#funcconvert"><em>Function description</em></a></p>

</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_hzar <a name="user-content-genepophzar"></a></h2><a id="user-content-genepop_hzar-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_hzar " href="#genepop_hzar-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">If you are interested in exploring clines in allele frequency over distance, you can convert from Genepop to HZAR format.This data can be used by the R package <a href="https://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/hzar/index.html" rel="nofollow">hzar</a> <a href="#funcconvert"><em>Function description</em></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#convert Genepop format to HZAR (.csz)

"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>convert Genepop format to HZAR (.csz)</span>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_flatten <a name="user-content-genepopflat"></a></h2><a id="user-content-genepop_flatten-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_flatten " href="#genepop_flatten-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Flatten your geneotype data for other calculations. This function will convert and return the genepop format into a dataframe. Because this function returns the dataframe, it needs to be assigned a variable ID. Note that this function does not have any subsetting capabilities. If you would like to remove loci and-or populations, this must be before hand using <em>subset_genepop</em> or its sister functions (see below for examples). <a href="#funcconvert"><em>Function description</em></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#Flatten the dataframe
  GenePop_df&lt;- genepop_flatten(GenePopData)

#inspect the output for the first 10 columns 
  head(GenePop_df[,1:10])"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>Flatten the dataframe</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">GenePop_df</span><span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> genepop_flatten(<span class="pl-smi">GenePopData</span>)

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>inspect the output for the first 10 columns </span>
  head(<span class="pl-smi">GenePop_df</span>[,<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-k">:</span><span class="pl-c1">10</span>])</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">genepop_unflatten <a name="user-content-genepopunflat"></a></h2><a id="user-content-genepop_unflatten-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: genepop_unflatten " href="#genepop_unflatten-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">If you are working with a flattened dataframe in your workspace you can convert it back to Genepop format. **Note that the first column of this data.frame should correspond to the sampleID (e.g. "BON_01") and the remaining columns should be Loci. <a href="#funcconvert"><em>Function description</em></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# create a Genepop format which can be used by other genepopedit functions

genepop_unflatten(<span class="pl-smi">GenePop_df</span>, <span class="pl-v">path</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> paste0(<span class="pl-smi">output_dir</span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>GenePop_UNFLATTENED.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>))</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto"><strong>Conversion using PGDspider</strong></h1><a id="user-content-conversion-using-pgdspider" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Conversion using PGDspider" href="#conversion-using-pgdspider"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">PGDspideR <a name="user-content-pgdspiderConvert"></a></h2><a id="user-content-pgdspider-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: PGDspideR " href="#pgdspider-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">There are a broad range of data formats which can be converted to and from using PGDspider. If you have multiple files which you are going to be converting using the same conversion parameters, <em>PGDspideR.R</em> can be useful, providing a code based interface to exploit the conversion functions of PGDspider. <a href="#funcpgd"><em>Function description</em></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#convert between GENEPOP and FSTAT format using PGDspider
  pgdSpideR(input = paste0(output_dir,&quot;Genepop_IDsubset.txt&quot;),
  input_format=&quot;GENEPOP&quot;,
  output = paste0(output_dir,&quot;Genepop_IDsubset_FSTAT.dat&quot;,
  output_format=&quot;FSTAT&quot;,
  spid=&quot;c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/spids/GENEPOP_FSTAT.spid&quot;,
  where.pgdspider=&quot;c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/PGDSpider_2.0.9.0/&quot;)
"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>convert between GENEPOP and FSTAT format using PGDspider</span>
  pgdSpideR(<span class="pl-v">input</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> paste0(<span class="pl-smi">output_dir</span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Genepop_IDsubset.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>),
  <span class="pl-v">input_format</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>GENEPOP<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,
  <span class="pl-v">output</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> paste0(<span class="pl-smi">output_dir</span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Genepop_IDsubset_FSTAT.dat<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,

  <span class="pl-v">spid</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/spids/GENEPOP_FSTAT.spid<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,
  <span class="pl-v">where.pgdspider</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>c:/Users/YOURNAME/Documents/Programs/PGDSpider_2.0.9.0/<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)
</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">#<strong>Simulate genotypes using pooled DNA allele frequencies</strong></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">alleleotype_genepop <a name="user-content-pooldna"></a></h2><a id="user-content-alleleotype_genepop-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: alleleotype_genepop " href="#alleleotype_genepop-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Individual geneotypes can be simulated using the <em>alleleotype_genepop()</em> function and formatted to GENEPOP for use in conventional genomic analyses (e.g. assigner, DAPC, STRUCTURE). This function will simulate individuals for each population provided by the input file. The output can then be diagnosed, sampled, and formatted using other <strong>genepopedit functions</strong>. <a href="#pooleddna"><em>Function description</em></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#simulate individual geneotypes allele frequencies stratified by population.
  #Create an example pooled DNA input file
    pooledDNA &lt;- data.frame(Pop = c(&quot;Pop1&quot;,&quot;Pop2&quot;,&quot;Pop3&quot;,&quot;Pop4&quot;,&quot;Pop5&quot;),Loci1 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci2 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci3 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci4 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci5 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2),Loci6 = round(runif(5, 0, 1),2))
    
    #inspect the input
    pooledDNA

  #simulate 200 individual geneotypes for each population
    alleleotype_genepop(pooledDNA, numsim = 200, path = paste0(output_dir,&quot;SimulatedGeneotypes.txt&quot;))
  
  #To validate output simulate 100 (default) geneotypes per population and compare allele frequencies to those of the input file. Estimated frequencies per population and SNP should match those of the input file within +/- 1%.
  
    alleleotype_genepop(pooledDNA, numsim = 100, path = paste0(output_dir,&quot;SimulatedGeneotypesValidate.txt&quot;))
   
    genepop_allelefreq(paste0(output_dir,&quot;SimulatedGeneotypesValidate.txt&quot;))
    
  #Note you can simulate new geneotypes using the summary from genepop_allelefreq(... , wide = TRUE).
    GeneFreq &lt;- genepop_allelefreq(&quot;Genepop_IDsubset.txt&quot;,wide = TRUE)
    
    alleleotype_genepop(GeneFreq, numsim = 100, path = paste0(output_dir,&quot;SimulatedGeneotypes_Genepop_IDsubset.txt&quot;))"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>simulate individual geneotypes allele frequencies stratified by population.</span>
